< Text>
We recently brought our dog in for a dental cleaning and mouth problem  because it seemed like she had a tooth issue and it maybe needed a removal judging by her behavior. We aren't foreign to this due to the fact that she has had several teeth pulled in the past (she just has bad teeth, we've tried everything to combat the issue) and we are very familiar with the signs. However, the vet seemed to think it was an intestinal issue and claimed that he saw nothing wrong, he barely examinedher mouth in front of us, he was so sure of himself that he didn't listen to us, the owners. So we were skeptical when we left, and had near insisted that it was her teeth and we felt they should have xrayed her mouth but they did not. After a week of antibiotics, nothing changed so we called and complained and they "squeezed us in" an additional week later, it should have been sooner and they should have made more of an effort to do so when I complained that the vet had overlooked the issue. When we brought her back they realize the  issue and at that point it had advanced horribly. There is no way that in one week her tooth and the gums around it would become so bad (they called it necrotic.) They had failed to listen to us when we insisted that it was a tooth problem (seeing as we had past experiences with the issue.)
Our poor dog had to suffer an extra two weeks due to them! She was REALLY bad and we couldn't afford to take her to the E.R. having just paid for her previous appointment and the body (excluding the head) xrays and medication they gave her. I did not berate her in front of the other customers, though I absolutely had the right to complain.
We are long time customers, but we are disgusted and dismayed by our experience and their lack of professionalism.
We are now shopping for a new vet.
We shall not be returning.<//Text>

< Review>
My family and I were going out of town for a trip and we needed to board our 2 year old lab. I've boarded her there before and had no problems, so we decided to book again. While on vacation, I received a call (not from San Joaquin) that my dog was running down Allen with no collar on (San Joaquin removes collars when boarding) and that the caller has my dog. Now, I didn't have service at the time of the call so I didn't know about this until a few hours later when I regained cell service. When I did regain cell service I found out the real series of events that took place. An employee at San Joaquin took my dog to the play area, while in the play area my dog somehow got out and instead of the employee going in to get help to get my dog back, they didn't mention anything. So no one, besides the employee responsible for my dog, knew she was missing. When the caller found my dog, she immediately took her to San Joaquin to see if she was chipped (because she had no collar on), which is how she got my information, the caller then took my dog back to her place of work (down the street from San Joaquin) for over 2 hours! Before someone from San Joaquin called her saying "ummm, I think the dog you have is supposed to be here with us". Now, I understand people make mistakes but what is the most frustrating from the whole situation is I NEVER received a call from San Joaquin, in fact, if the caller would not have told me what happened, I would have never known! They would have not told me and pretended as if it never happened. The manager did inform me the employee was fired (not my intention) and didn't charge me for my dog's stay (not my intention either). I'm a pretty understanding person but to not even get a courtesy call after losing my dog for over 2 hours after she was running down Allen with no collar was just unacceptable to me. Needless to say, I won't be boarding my animals there any time soon!< /Review>

<review>A friend of ours told us that Bella Roma was much improved after the last time they changed hands, and we finally got around to giving it a try.  I'd give it 2.5 stars if I could, but I'm afraid I have to round it down.

The pizza itself was three stars ('it's okay") -- it wasn't phenomenal, but it was at least pretty good.  However, it seemed like they were skimpy on the toppings, especially the cheese; while it's not unusual for our kids not to eat the crust, there was a large zone next to the crust that only had sauce, which our kids also wouldn't eat.  It seemed quite overpriced for what we got.

What drives the rating down, though, was the ordering experience.  We tried it because the coupon bundle we'd received in the mail the day before had coupons for Bella Roma, and we decided to go for the "2 large, 2-topping pizzas for $29.99", and planned to do half-and-half on them (half with cheese only, and 2 different toppings on each of the other halves).  When I called, I was told that there was no such deal.  When I said I was looking right at the coupon sheet that just came in the mail, he said that they must have misprinted it, and they wouldn't honor it.

He then told me (not asked, told) that I should use the better deal -- one cheese pizza, and one supreme (or up to 4 toppings) for $28.99.  Well, that's not really the same, is it?  I want at most two toppings on each half, not 4 toppings anywhere.

But I went along with it, and had him add two toppings to half of the cheese (for more, of course).  Then when I told him what I wanted on the halves of the other pizza, he told me (with attitude) that their computer wouldn't let him do halves.  Seriously?  Yeah, try it on their website -- they can do half-and-half pizzas, but not as part of the special.  Fine, give me the same two toppings on the whole thing.  If I'd known how skimpy they'd be on the cheese, I would have added extra cheese -- oh, wait, they don't offer it.

We went ahead with it because the kids were hungry and crazy, and because we were expecting great pizza.  I wish I'd listened to my gut, which was telling me to be put off by the attitude I was getting on the phone.  After being told brusquely that I couldn't get what I wanted (which didn't seem unreasonable), I ended up with mediocre pizza.  Not bad enough to drop it to one star, but we won't be going back.<//review><response>None<//response>< rate>

< Review>
Their pizza is really good and I've ordered from them 1 time before and that was only for cheese just to try them out.

For this particular experience was different for me since I'm not quite sure how they're pizzas are made. Under the pizza where it says "special instructions," I requested "No tomatoes," and still got tomatoes on my pizza. I understand if the pizzas are pre-made and they can't do anything about that, but if they add the toppings on themselves, then they should be aware of when special requests are made and not add tomatoes when a customer requests none. In my opinion, I feel like there should be a customizable function for customers who want to edit their orders, but there's no feature for that. And I don't know if my pizza was actually deep dish or not since it looked like a normal pizza to me where I thought all deep dish pizzas were like a rectangular shape.

I also added Mug Rootbeer where I don't mind this brand either, but realized that I got A&W instead where it made me think that they could be sold out of Mug Rootbeer which is understandable. But if they were actually sold out of Mug Rootbeer, then that should have been specified. Idk if they've ever had Mug Rootbeer, but if they haven't, then their website needs to be updated. I totally understand that most likely the staff who work at the store has no control over the website, but for the website: please advertise what you actually have in store. I gave it 4 stars because their pizza is still delicious nonetheless despite this experience of mine.< /Review>

My cousin suggested this food truck while we were all sitting around thinking about what to get for dinner, we get to where the truck is parked (always in the same location) there was about 3 people in line. I guess it's a spin on "benihana" ...I've never been to benihana so I can't speak to its similarities or differences. I ordered chicken and shrimp and a side of filet mignon. Which cost $30 bucksüòü  I got about 4 pieces of shrimp and my fillet mignon was toughüò©. Not to much flavor but it wasn't bad. I ordered chicken and shrimp and a side of filet mignon. Which cost $30 bucksüòü  I got about 4 pieces of shrimp and my fillet mignon was toughüò©. Not to much flavor but it wasn't bad. It was definitely a healthier option and was pretty decent but definitely not worth $30.</text>

< review>
By far the worst rental experience I have ever had. I rented a truck from them, purchased every single insurance that they offered, and the damage wasn't covered at all. Not a single cent. When they initially contacted me about the damage, they claimed it would not exceed $1500, which was what the deductible was for their insurance. I was willing to accept that, but just got the bill today and nope, not even close.  I am being billed almost $2800 dollars for damage. But I guess I should expect this type of conduct after talking with a friend that used to work there who said that Avon makes a profit off of accidents.

If you're a production company, Avon MAY work with you. But if you're an individual, don't EVER rent from them. Their rates seem reasonable at first (until all the taxes and fees add up), but they're insurance is a complete scam. I will never use Avon again, and will urge all of my friends in the industry to use Galpin Studio Rentals instead.< /review>

I rented the Hybrid Diesel Electric box truck for 10 days and would highly recommend it!
